<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Euler Flexural Buckling of Cantilever I Beam under Axial Compression
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: beam_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This benchmark problem investigates the classical Euler flexural buckling of a slender cantilever beam subjected to uniform axial compression. The objective is to determine the critical buckling load and associated flexural mode shape using a linear eigenvalue buckling analysis, and to evaluate the postbuckling response using a geometrically nonlinear procedure.

The structure consists of a straight prismatic beam of length 12 m aligned along the global x-axis. The cross-section is a doubly symmetric I-section with flange width 300 mm, flange thickness 27 mm, web thickness 14.5 mm, and overall depth 690 mm. The material is assumed to be homogeneous, isotropic, and linearly elastic, with Young’s modulus equal to 211 GPa and Poisson’s ratio equal to 0.3125.

All translational and rotational degrees of freedom are restrained at one end of the beam, forming a cantilever configuration. An axial compressive load is applied at the free end. The beam is discretized using open-section beam elements suitable for instability analysis.

An eigenvalue buckling procedure is performed to obtain the critical load multiplier and corresponding flexural mode shape. To study the nonlinear response beyond the critical point, a Riks analysis may be carried out by introducing an initial geometric imperfection proportional to the lowest eigenmode. This benchmark provides validation for flexural buckling prediction of slender columns and comparison with classical Euler theory.
</problem_description>
<input_file>
*HEADING

*RESTART,WRITE,FREQUENCY=999

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Lateral Torsional Buckling of Simply Supported I Beam under Transverse Distributed Load
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: beam_under_flexural_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This benchmark problem examines the lateral–torsional instability of a slender I-section beam subjected to transverse distributed loading. The objective is to determine the critical load associated with lateral buckling and to assess the postbuckling response and imperfection sensitivity.

The beam is 12 m long and aligned with the global x-axis. The cross-section is a doubly symmetric I-section with flange width 300 mm, flange thickness 27 mm, web thickness 14.5 mm, and total depth 690 mm. The material is linear elastic and isotropic with Young’s modulus of 211 GPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3125.

The beam is simply supported. At one support, all translational degrees of freedom and rotation about the longitudinal axis are restrained. At the other support, transverse displacements and axial rotation are restrained. A uniformly distributed transverse load is applied in the vertical direction.

An eigenvalue buckling analysis is first conducted to compute the critical load multiplier and lateral–torsional buckling mode. A subsequent nonlinear load–displacement analysis using the Riks method may be performed by introducing a small initial imperfection derived from the first eigenmode. The benchmark demonstrates instability behavior of open thin-walled beams subjected to bending and highlights the influence of geometric imperfections on collapse.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Pure Torsional Buckling of Slender I Beam under Axial Compression
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: beam_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This benchmark problem studies torsional instability of a slender open-section beam subjected to axial compression. The objective is to determine the torsional critical load using a linear eigenvalue buckling analysis and to identify the governing instability mode.

The beam is straight, 12 m in length, and oriented along the global x-axis. The cross-section is a doubly symmetric I-section with flange width 300 mm, flange thickness 27 mm, web thickness 14.5 mm, and total depth 690 mm. Due to its open thin-walled geometry, the section possesses relatively low torsional rigidity compared to closed sections.

The material is homogeneous, isotropic, and linearly elastic with Young’s modulus of 211 GPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3125. A concentrated axial compressive load is applied at one end of the beam. Appropriate boundary conditions are applied to permit torsional deformation while preventing rigid body motion.

An eigenvalue buckling procedure is used to extract the torsional mode shape and corresponding critical load factor. This benchmark provides validation for torsional buckling prediction of open thin-walled beams and allows comparison between flexural and torsional instability modes.

</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Eigenvalue Buckling Prediction of Cylindrical Shell Ring Segment with Mode Number Sweep
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: cylindrical_shell_under_axial_compression
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
The problem consists of a long, thin, metal cylinder that is simply supported at its ends and subjected to a uniformly distributed compressive axial stress. The cylinder is sufficiently slender so that buckling occurs well below the material yield limit, and the response remains entirely in the elastic range.

In the case studied, the cylinder has a length of 20.32 m (800 in), a radius of 2.54 m (100 in), and a shell thickness of 6.35 mm (0.25 in). The resulting radius-to-thickness ratio is 400:1, indicating a very thin shell that is highly susceptible to instability. The shell is made of an isotropic material with Young’s modulus equal to 207 GPa (30 × 10^6 lb/in^2) and Poisson’s ratio equal to 0.3.

An eigenvalue buckling analysis is performed to estimate the bifurcation load multiplier and the associated buckling mode shape. Because of the symmetry of the geometry, only a segment of the cylinder is modeled rather than the full circumference. The circumferential extent of the model corresponds to one-quarter of a circumferential wave and subtends an angle alpha = pi / (2n), where n is the number of circumferential waves in the complete cylinder. By varying n, the critical buckling stress associated with different circumferential wave patterns can be determined.

Along the axial direction, only half of the cylinder length is modeled. Symmetry or antisymmetry boundary conditions are applied at the midlength plane to capture even or odd longitudinal half-wave numbers m. This reduced modeling approach significantly lowers computational cost while accurately representing the global instability behavior.

In this benchmark case, the mesh is defined using S4R5 shell elements. The eigenvalue buckling procedure in Abaqus is used to compute the load multiplier at which the structure reaches instability.
Given Input File : bucklecylshell_s4r5_n1.inp
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Eigenvalue prediction of buckling of a simply supported square plate
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
Model a thin, flat square plate of side length (b) in the global (x)–(y) plane with edges parallel to the coordinate axes, and take advantage of symmetry so that only the upper-right quarter of the plate is analyzed ((0\le x\le b/2,;0\le y\le b/2)) using a finer shell mesh of 4×4 elements over the quarter). 
Impose symmetry boundary conditions on the two cut edges: on the edge (x=0) set (u_x=0) and (\phi_y=\phi_z=0), and on the edge (y=0) set (u_y=0) and (\phi_x=\phi_z=0). Apply simple support conditions on the two outer edges of the quarter model to represent simple support on all four edges of the full plate: 
on the edge (x=b/2) set (u_z=0) and (\phi_x=0), and on the edge (y=b/2) set (u_z=0) and (\phi_y=0). Apply uniform mechanical compressive edge loading on the two opposite full-plate edges parallel to the (y)-axis; in the quarter model this is applied along the outer edge (x=b/2) as a compressive load acting 
in the negative (x) direction, using any convenient reference magnitude because the eigenvalue buckling procedure scales linearly with the applied load. Request several eigenmodes and use the lowest eigenvalue as the buckling load estimate, with the analytical reference (N_{crit}=4\pi^2D/b^2), 
where (D=Et^3/[12(1-\nu^2)]), and the corresponding mode shape (w=A\cos(\pi x/b)\cos(\pi y/b)). Use the benchmark parameters (b=2), plate thickness (t=0.01), and an isotropic linear elastic material with (E=10^8) and (\nu=0.3), assuming a consistent set of units throughout.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Load–displacement response of a simply supported square plate under edge compression
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case predicts the nonlinear edge load–out-of-plane displacement response of a thin, flat, square metal plate that is simply supported along all four edges and compressed in-plane along one pair of opposite edges. The plate first deforms in-plane, then loses stability and develops out-of-plane deflection (buckling). The response is captured using a static nonlinear step with geometric nonlinearity enabled so the postbuckling path can be followed.

Geometry
A flat square plate with side length L and uniform thickness t (t is much smaller than L). The mid-surface lies in the global X–Y plane, and the plate normal is the global Z direction. The model is a full plate (no symmetry reduction) so the buckling mode is not artificially constrained.

Boundary conditions (simply supported plate)
All four edges are simply supported to represent line supports:
- Out-of-plane displacement is constrained on all edges: U3 = 0 on all boundary edges.
- Rotations about tangential directions are left free (no clamping moments).
- In-plane rigid-body motion is removed with minimal constraints:
  - One corner (or a single reference node) is fixed in U1 and U2 to prevent rigid translation.
  - A second point is constrained in one in-plane direction (U2 or U1) to prevent rigid rotation in-plane.
These constraints stabilize the model without adding artificial stiffness.

Loading and output (load–displacement)
In-plane compression is applied along one pair of opposite edges (for example, the +X edge is pushed toward the −X edge) using one of the following equivalent approaches:
- Prescribed edge displacement (recommended for stable postbuckling): apply U1 = −Δ on the loaded edge while the opposite edge has U1 = 0, and then compute the reaction force vs. out-of-plane displacement; or
- Applied uniform edge load/traction: apply compressive line load or distributed traction on the loaded edge and track equilibrium with nonlinear geometry.
The primary response curve is obtained as:
- Total edge reaction force (sum of RF1 on the constrained/loaded edge) versus
- Representative out-of-plane displacement (U3) at the plate center (or at a defined monitoring point).

Analysis procedure
A static nonlinear step with geometric nonlinearity (NLGEOM=YES) is used. To trigger buckling in a stable way, a small initial imperfection is introduced (typically by seeding the plate with a scaled first buckling mode shape from a prior eigenvalue analysis, or by a small initial out-of-plane perturbation at the center). Automatic stabilization or arc-length (Riks) may be used if snap-through or unstable equilibrium is expected.

Elements (recommended)
Shell elements are recommended for thin plates:
- S4R as the default (good accuracy and robust convergence)
- S8R if higher accuracy is required for mode shape and stiffness
A structured quad mesh with refinement near edges/corners is typically used.

</problem_description>
<input_file>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Eigenvalue Buckling of a ring in a plane under external pressure
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: annular
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case predicts the asymmetric buckling of a thin elastic ring in a plane under uniform external pressure using an eigenvalue buckling procedure. The prebuckling deformation is axisymmetric, but buckling occurs in a periodic circumferential mode with mode number k, where the lowest critical mode is typically k = 2. Because the k = 2 mode can be represented by a reduced circumferential sector, a 45° ring segment model is commonly used for an efficient eigenvalue buckling estimate.

Geometry
The structure is a circular ring of mean radius R lying in the global X–Y plane, with its center at the origin. The ring has a uniform square cross-section with side a (a × a) around the circumference. Benchmark values are R = 2.54 m (100 in) and a = 25.4 mm (1 in). The circumferential location is described by the angle θ measured from the global X axis.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic metal with Young’s modulus E and Poisson’s ratio ν. Benchmark materials properties are E = 206.8 GPa (30 × 10^6 lb/in^2) and ν = 0.3  (modify here based on user requirement)

Loading (dummy pressure for easy modification)
A uniform external pressure acts radially inward on the ring. In eigenvalue buckling, Abaqus returns a load multiplier, so the absolute pressure magnitude can be set to a dummy reference value such as p0 = 1.0 (model units) or p0 = 6895 Pa (1 psi). The user can later replace p0 with any required pressure level and compute the critical pressure as pcr = (eigenvalue) × p0.

Boundary conditions
A reduced circumferential sector model is used. Symmetry conditions are applied at θ = 0°. At the sector boundary (for example θ = 45°), a local radial–tangential coordinate system is defined so constraints can be applied in local directions. During the preload (axisymmetric compression under pressure) the sector boundary uses symmetric conditions, but during eigenvalue extraction the sector boundary conditions are switched to antisymmetric so the selected circumferential buckling mode can form in the reduced model. In Abaqus this is implemented by specifying a second boundary-condition set (LOAD CASE = 2) that is active only during the *BUCKLE procedure. Minimal additional constraints are included only to remove rigid-body motion without adding artificial stiffness.

Analysis procedure
An eigenvalue buckling step (*BUCKLE) is used to extract the lowest buckling eigenvalue and corresponding mode shape based on the stiffness state under the applied pressure. Typically only the first mode is needed when the sector is chosen specifically to represent k = 2; additional modes can be requested if desired.

Output request
Requested outputs include the buckling eigenvalue(s) (load multipliers) and eigenmode shape(s) to confirm the circumferential mode, along with nodal displacements and reaction forces (U, RF) to verify boundary conditions. Standard field output can be included for visualization of the buckling deformation.
</problem_description>
<input_file>

<index>
case name: Dynamic buckling of an X-shaped column with general contact
case domain: dynamic_analysis_not_vibration_analysis
case category: solid_column_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
Dynamic buckling analysis of a thin-walled steel column with an X-shaped cross-section in Abaqus/Explicit. The column is placed between two rigid platens. The bottom platen is fixed. The top platen undergoes axial compression and a 31° rotation over 7 msec.

Geometry
Column height: 1.0 m
Cross-section: X-shaped, four flanges
Flange width: 0.2 m
Flange thickness: 0.003 m
Rigid platens at top and bottom

Material
Steel, elastic–perfectly plastic:
Young’s modulus: 200 GPa
Poisson’s ratio: 0.3
Density: 7850 kg/m³
Yield stress: 250 MPa

Boundary conditions
Node-based surface at each column end
Each surface tied to corresponding rigid platen
Bottom platen: fixed
Top platen: prescribed axial displacement + 31° rotation in 7 msec

Contact definition
Abaqus/Explicit general contact
General contact inclusions used to define an all-inclusive surface
Captures column self-contact and column–platen contact
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Laminated strip under three-point bending
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: beam_under_flexural_loading
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model reproduces the NAFEMS R0031/1 laminated strip benchmark using a composite shell formulation (S8R) to predict midspan bending response and key stress measures. Only the composite S8R shell model is described here.

Geometry and coordinate system
The strip is a straight rectangular beam.
Length L = 50 mm (global x direction).
Width b = 10 mm (global y direction).
Total thickness t = 1 mm (global z direction, defined by composite shell section).
The quarter model represents 0 ≤ x ≤ 25 mm and 0 ≤ y ≤ 5 mm using symmetry at x = 25 mm and y = 0 mm.

Laminate layup (through thickness)
A symmetric laminate is defined using a composite shell section. The total thickness is 1.0 mm with the following ply stack (top to bottom):
0.1 mm at 0°
0.1 mm at 90°
0.1 mm at 0°
0.4 mm at 90°
0.1 mm at 0°
0.1 mm at 90°
0.1 mm at 0°
The 0° fiber direction is aligned with the beam length (global x direction).

Material (orthotropic lamina)
E1 = 100 GPa, E2 = 5 GPa, ν12 = 0.4, G12 = 3 GPa, G13 = 2 GPa, G23 = 2 GPa.
For the composite shell section, these are provided as lamina engineering constants in the Abaqus lamina definition.

Boundary conditions
Simply supported at A and B (support lines). In the shell model this is implemented by restraining the transverse displacement uz along the support lines while leaving rotations free. Symmetry constraints are applied on the quarter model planes (y = 0 and x = 25) to enforce the quarter symmetry representation.

Loading
A downward line load of 10 N/mm is applied at point C located at x = 25 mm on the top surface (z = 1 mm). In the quarter model, this line load is applied along the line at x = 25 mm over the modeled half width (0 ≤ y ≤ 5 mm) using equivalent nodal loads.

Mesh (S8R)
The benchmark mesh for general purpose quadratic shell models uses:
5 elements along the length direction of the quarter model (0 ≤ x ≤ 25 mm), and
1 element along the breadth direction of the quarter model (0 ≤ y ≤ 5 mm).
Element type is S8R with a composite section definition.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Wrapped thick cylinder under pressure and thermal loading
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This benchmark evaluates a wrapped thick cylinder under internal pressure and combined pressure plus thermal loading using an Abaqus Standard composite shell formulation (S8R). The goal is to capture the global deformation and the stress distribution in a two material cylinder made of an inner isotropic tube and an outer circumferentially wound orthotropic wrap, consistent with NAFEMS Test 2.

Geometry and model extent
The structure is a thick walled cylinder with total length 200 mm. A reduced model is used:

1. one quarter of the cylinder cross section (symmetry in the cross sectional plane)
2. one half of the cylinder length (symmetry in the axial direction)
The axial coordinate is z. The constrained end is at z = 0. All dimensions are in mm.

Element type and section definition (Composite S8R only)
The cylinder is modeled using S8R shell elements with a composite shell section to represent the layered construction. The inner metal tube and the outer wrap are represented as distinct layers within the composite section. A cylindrical material orientation is assigned to the wrapped layer so that material direction 1 follows the circumferential (hoop) direction, representing circumferential winding.

Mesh (benchmark mesh rule for this model type)
For the composite S8R model, the benchmark uses the “quadratic solids and general purpose shells” mesh density:
4 elements along the radial direction and 4 elements along the axial direction for the reduced model domain.

Through thickness representation (S8R composite section)
The thickness is represented by a composite shell section definition, not by stacking separate continuum layers. The composite section includes:

1. the inner isotropic cylinder layer
2. the outer orthotropic wrapped layer

Materials
Inner isotropic cylinder:
E = 2.1E5 MPa
nu = 0.3
alpha = 2.0e-5 per degree C

Outer circumferentially wound wrap (orthotropic with thermal expansion):
E1 = 130 GPa
E2 = 5 GPa
E3 = 5 GPa
nu12 = 0.25
nu13 = 0.25
nu23 = 0.0
G12 = 10 GPa
G13 = 10 GPa
G23 = 5 GPa
alpha11 = 3.0e-6 per degree C
alpha22 = 2.0e-5 per degree C
alpha33 = 2.0e-5 per degree C

Boundary conditions
Axial displacement is constrained at the end surface:
uz = 0 at z = 0
Symmetry boundary conditions are applied to represent one quarter of the cross section and one half of the cylinder length. Only minimal additional constraints are used to prevent rigid body motion.

Loading cases
Case 1:
Internal pressure p = 200 MPa applied to the inner surface (shell pressure load).

Case 2 (Abaqus Standard only):
Internal pressure p = 200 MPa plus a uniform temperature rise of DeltaT = 130 degrees C applied to the model.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Three layer sandwich shell under normal pressure loading
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: flat_plate
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
(NAFEMS Test 3, three layer sandwich plate under uniform normal pressure, Abaqus Standard, composite S8R)

Model intent
This benchmark models a three layer sandwich plate subjected to a uniform normal pressure. The objective is to reproduce the NAFEMS Test 3 response using a composite shell formulation (S8R) and to compare the predicted stress field with the benchmark reference.

Geometry and model extent
The structure is a square plate with in plane dimensions 10 in × 10 in in the global x y plane. The sandwich thickness is represented through a composite shell section consisting of two thin face sheets separated by a thick core. A quarter model is used for efficiency, with symmetry planes aligned with the plate midlines.

Element type and mesh (Composite S8R only)
The plate is discretized using composite S8R shell elements in Abaqus Standard. The quarter model uses a 4 × 4 mesh of S8R elements, consistent with the benchmark definition for the Abaqus Standard composite shell model.

Section layup (three layer composite shell section)
A composite shell section is assigned to the S8R elements to represent the sandwich construction. The layup is symmetric:
Top face sheet: thickness 0.028 in, material FACE
Core: thickness 0.750 in, material CORE
Bottom face sheet: thickness 0.028 in, material FACE
Total thickness is 0.806 in. Each layer is defined as a lamina in the composite shell section.

Materials
Face sheets (orthotropic lamina, used in FACE layers):
E1 = 1.0 × 10^7 psi
E2 = 4.0 × 10^6 psi
nu12 = 0.3
G12 = 1.875 × 10^6 psi
G13 = 1.875 × 10^6 psi
G23 = 1.875 × 10^6 psi

Core (orthotropic lamina, used in CORE layer):
E1 = 10 psi
E2 = 10 psi
nu12 = 0
G12 = 10 psi
G13 = 3.0 × 10^4 psi
G23 = 1.2 × 10^4 psi
In continuum shell variants of this benchmark, thickness moduli may be increased to avoid pinching effects, but this S8R composite shell model uses the lamina constants as defined.

Boundary conditions (simply supported on all four edges)
The plate is simply supported along all four edges. In the composite shell model this is implemented by restraining transverse displacement along the boundary edges while applying minimal in plane constraints only to remove rigid body motion, consistent with a simply supported plate assumption.

Loading
A uniform normal pressure of 100 psi is applied over the plate surface using a shell pressure load.
</problem_description>

case name: Axisymmetric branched shell under pressure

<problem_description>
Model an axisymmetric shell in the r z plane with constant thickness 0.01 m. The midsurface profile has two connected parts: a quarter circle arc and a straight vertical segment. Start at point B on the axis of symmetry (r = 0). Create a quarter circle arc of radius 1.0 m that ends at point C on a vertical line at radius r = 1 over sqrt(2) m. From point C, continue with a straight vertical line up to point D. The vertical distance from A to C is 1.0 m and from C to D is 1.0 m, so the total vertical height from A to D is 2.0 m. Point A is the bottom of the right vertical segment at the same radius as C and D, located 1.0 m below point C.

Element
SAX2 axisymmetric shell element. Use the fine mesh discretization only.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 210 GPa
nu = 0.3

Boundary conditions
At point A, restrain the axisymmetric shell degrees of freedom to prevent rigid body motion:
ur = 0
uz = 0
phi = 0

Loading
Apply a uniform internal pressure of 1.0 MPa along the boundary B C D, acting normal to the shell edge (pressure directed from the inside toward the shell).

<index>
case name: Axisymmetric cylinder/sphere under internal pressure

<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models a thin walled axisymmetric pressure vessel made of a cylindrical shell with a spherical head, subjected to uniform internal pressure. The model is defined in the r z plane and revolved about the z axis to represent the full 3D vessel. Units are m and kN, and the shell thickness is constant with thickness = 0.025 m.

Geometry described by the figure
The midsurface profile consists of two connected parts:

1. a curved spherical head from point A to point B
2. a straight cylindrical wall from point B down to point F at constant radius r = 1.0 m

The cylindrical segment lies on the right side of the figure (vertical line at r = 1.0 m). The spherical head connects smoothly into this cylinder near the top. The total vertical extent shown is 2.5 m, with the upper head region occupying the top 1.0 m and the cylindrical region extending downward 1.5 m to point F. Reference points B, D, and E are located on or near the cylinder line, and their r and z coordinates are provided in the figure for stress and displacement checks.

Element and mesh (fine mesh only)
Use SAX2 axisymmetric shell elements. Only the fine mesh discretization from the input file nle7xa3f.inp is used.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 210 GPa
nu = 0.3
density = 7800 kg/m3

Boundary conditions
Apply constraints to prevent rigid body motion using the benchmark point definitions:
At point A: ur = 0 and phi = 0
At point F: uz = 0

Loading
Apply a uniform internal pressure of 1.0 MPa on the inner surface of the vessel. For explicit dynamic variants of this benchmark, the pressure is ramped to obtain a quasi static response. In this case the load history follows the definition in nle7xa3f.inp.
</problem_description>

case name: Skew plate under normal pressure

<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models a thin skew plate subjected to a uniform transverse pressure. The plate is a four sided parallelogram (skew plate) with constant thickness 0.01 m. The geometry has two pairs of opposite edges that are straight and parallel, producing interior angles of 30 degrees at two opposite corners and 150 degrees at the other two corners. The objective is to evaluate bending response of a skew plate under normal pressure using shell elements and a fine mesh discretization.

Element and mesh (S4R, fine mesh only)
Use S4R shell elements. Only the fine mesh input file le6_f.inp is used (fine 4 × 4 mesh for this benchmark definition).

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 210 GPa
nu = 0.3
density = 7800 kg/m3

Boundary conditions
All four edges are simply supported by restraining the out of plane displacement along the entire boundary. To prevent rigid body motion in the plate plane, the in plane displacements are constrained at two corner points:

at corner A: fix both in plane displacement components

at corner B: fix one in plane displacement component while leaving the other free

Loading
Apply a uniform pressure of 7.0 kPa normal to the plate surface in the downward direction. For explicit dynamic variants of this benchmark, the pressure is ramped slowly to obtain a quasi static response, but this case follows the loading definition in le6_f.inp.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: free vibration analysis of a clamped thin rhombic plate

<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case computes the natural frequencies and mode shapes of a thin clamped rhombic plate using a shell based eigenfrequency extraction. The physical plate has planform dimensions 10 m by 10 m with uniform thickness and lies in the global x y plane, with the z direction normal to the surface. A local in plane coordinate system is defined by rotating the global x y axes by 45 degrees about the z axis. The rotated axes x prime and y prime lie in the plate plane and are used to describe the rhombic orientation, while the local z prime axis remains normal to the plate.

Element and input file (S8R5 only)
Use S8R5 shell elements and the model definition from input file nfv1558x.inp.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 200 GPa
nu = 0.3
density = 8000 kg/m3

Boundary conditions
The plate is fully clamped along all four edges. Along the boundary edges:

1. out of plane displacement is restrained
2. rotations about the in plane axes are restrained
   To eliminate any remaining rigid body motion for the shell model, in plane translations in x and y are restrained and the drilling rotation about the z axis is fixed as defined in the input file.

Analysis type (free vibration)
No external loads are applied. An eigenfrequency extraction (modal) step is performed to compute natural frequencies and corresponding mode shapes from the plate mass and stiffness.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: Compact tension specimen
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models a 2D compact tension type specimen in plane strain style geometry using a single reference size w = 50 mm. The outline is constructed from straight line segments in the global x y plane (x to the right, y upward). Derived dimensions are:
h = 0.6w = 30 mm
a = 0.5w = 25 mm
a prime = 0.2a = 5 mm
h prime = 0.6h = 18 mm
h double prime = 0.25h = 7.5 mm
w prime = 1.25w = 62.5 mm

Geometry construction (full outline definition)
Start at point A at (x = w, y = 0).

1. Right edge: go vertically to (w, h).
2. Top edge: go left to (w minus w prime, h).
3. Left edge: go down by h prime to (w minus w prime, h minus h prime).
4. Upper step: go right by a prime to (w minus w prime plus a prime, h minus h prime).
5. Lower step: go down by h double prime to (w minus w prime plus a prime, h minus h prime minus h double prime).
6. Ligament edge: go horizontally to the right until point B at (x = w minus a, y = 0).
7. Bottom edge: close the outline from B to A along y = 0.

The crack or notch tip is the re entrant corner at the step transition, and the mesh is refined in this region. Collapsed quarter point elements are used at the crack tip by shifting midside nodes to the quarter point location.

Element and model extent (CPE8 only)
Use CPE8 quadratic plane strain elements. Only half of the specimen is modeled by applying symmetry about the appropriate vertical centerline, consistent with the benchmark input file nlf6xf8x.inp.

Mesh
A focused mesh is used around the crack tip with collapsed quarter point elements. The remaining region uses a structured quadratic mesh appropriate for the half geometry.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 207 GPa
nu = 0.3

Boundary conditions
Apply a roller type constraint along the bottom edge segment from B to A so that vertical displacement is zero along that edge. To prevent rigid body motion, also fix the horizontal displacement at point A.

Loading
Apply a concentrated vertical force P = 1000 N at the specified load point on the top edge (load line), acting upward to open the crack.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: Axisymmetric crack in a bar
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category: solid_column_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models an axisymmetric solid bar with a radial crack using the r z plane. The bar has outer radius R = 20 mm and height h = 1.5R = 30 mm. A radial crack of length b = 0.5R = 10 mm is located on the bottom face and extends inward from the outer surface, from r = R to r = R minus b at z = 0. Because the model is axisymmetric, only the r z cross section is meshed and revolved about the z axis.

Geometry definition (r z plane)
Define the rectangular bar cross section:
A at (r = 0, z = 0)
D at (r = R, z = 0)
C at (r = R, z = h)
B at (r = 0, z = h)

Define the crack on the bottom edge:
Crack mouth at (r = R, z = 0)
Crack tip at (r = R minus b, z = 0)

Element and input file (CAX8 only)
Use CAX8 quadratic axisymmetric continuum elements as defined in input file nlf5xf8x.inp. The crack tip region is modeled with collapsed quarter point elements by shifting midside nodes to the quarter point location using the singular element option.

Mesh (half axisymmetric model with crack tip singularity)
A focused mesh is used at the crack tip with collapsed quarter point elements. The remaining domain is meshed with structured CAX8 elements. The input file defines the crack tip node set TIP and uses NFILL with SINGULAR=1 to generate the quarter point singular mesh.

Material
Linear elastic isotropic:
E = 207000 MPa
nu = 0.3

Boundary conditions
Axis of symmetry (r = 0): restrain radial displacement ur = 0.
Bottom ligament segment (from r = 0 to r = R minus b at z = 0): restrain axial displacement uz = 0.
These constraints are applied via node sets consistent with the input file.

Loading
Apply a uniform tensile stress of 100 N per mm^2 in the axial direction on the top edge (z = h). In the input file, this is applied as a pressure type load in the axial direction on the element set PULL.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Viscoelastic rod subjected to constant axial load

<file_content>
<problem_description>
A viscoelastic circular rod is analyzed for its time-dependent axial response under a suddenly applied constant load. The rod is 254 mm long and 25.4 mm in diameter. The viscoelastic behavior is represented by a spring–dashpot rheological model (a standard linear solid), using two elastic springs and one dashpot to capture instantaneous elasticity and creep over time. The rod is modeled as an axisymmetric solid using a single quadratic hybrid axisymmetric element (CAX8H).

The same problem is also treated as a large-strain example. The relaxation behavior is defined in the same way, but the short-term elastic properties are given using hyperelastic behavior. The polynomial formulation with 
N
=
1 is used, and the constants are 
C
10
=

C

=

D
1
=
 1.378 × 10−7 MPa−1 (0.00002 psi−1). These constants are such that the initial Young's modulus and initial Poisson's ratio are equal to 
E

0
, respectively, and produce a close fit to a linear material. (See Hyperelastic Behavior of Rubberlike Materials for further discussion of the choice of constants when 
N
=
1.)


Loading
A distributed load of 0.689 MPa (100 psi) is applied instantaneously and held constant throughout the analysis. To model this, we use the quasi-static procedure (Quasi-Static Analysis) in two steps. The load is applied in the first step, which has a time period of 0.001 seconds, so that the instantaneous (glassy) behavior dominates. Since this step uses only one increment, a tolerance to control the accuracy of the creep integration is not specified. The second step has a time period of 50 seconds, during which the load is held constant and the rod is allowed to relax toward its long-term behavior. Automatic time incrementation is chosen by giving a tolerance value for the maximum difference in the creep strain increment over a time increment. This tolerance is selected so that its value is of the same order of magnitude as the maximum elastic strain. Therefore, for this example the tolerance is set to 5 × 10−3. The total force and the total moment on the loaded face of the model are output to the results file.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Transient thermal loading of a viscoelastic slab
case domain: dynamic_analysis_not_vibration_analysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: polymer
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
The example, taken from Collingwood et al. (1985), models a viscoelastic slab under plane strain restrained in all directions in its plane and examines the response of the slab after the temperature of its faces is raised suddenly to 100°.

The slab has unit half-thickness. Since the problem is one-dimensional, the slab is modeled with a single row of plane strain continuum elements. In Abaqus/Standard a sequential thermal-stress analysis is performed with two-dimensional, 8-node heat transfer elements, DC2D8, used for the heat transfer analysis and the corresponding 8-node plane strain continuum elements, CPE8R, used for the stress analysis. The mesh is shown in Figure 1. In Abaqus/Explicit a coupled thermal-stress analysis is performed using first-order plane strain elements (CPE3T and CPE4RT) to model the slab. Twenty elements are used along the length of the slab in the Abaqus/Explicit simulation.

The initial temperature throughout the slab is 0°. The outside face of the slab, at 
X
=
 1, is instantaneously raised to 100°. The mesh (Figure 1) is finer toward 
X
=
 1, where the temperature gradient is expected to be highest. The resulting transient temperature distribution is written to the results file and used as input to the subsequent stress analysis. Plane strain is imposed in the Y-direction by setting 
u
y
=
 0 on the two faces of the mesh at 
Y
=
 0 and 
Y
=
 1. Symmetry about 
X
=
 0 is also imposed.


Material
The thermal material properties are arbitrarily defined (in consistent units) as thermal conductivity (k) of 1.0, specific heat (c) of 1.0, and density (
ρ
) of 1.0.

The viscoelastic material models (small-strain and large-strain) are the same as the ones used in Viscoelastic rod subjected to constant axial load, with the addition of a temperature-time shift. The temperature-time shift uses the Williams-Landel-Ferry approximation,

log
(
A
)
=
−
C
1
(
θ
−
θ
0
)
C
2
+
(
θ
−
θ
0
)
,
where 
θ
0
 is the reference temperature at which the relaxation data are given and 
C
1
, 
C
2
 are calibration constants obtained at this temperature (for additional information on the WLF equation, see Viscoelasticity). When 
θ
≤
θ
0
−
C
2
,
 the material behavior is elastic. In this example 
C
1
=
 4.92, 
C
2
=
 215.0°, and 
θ
0
=
 70°. The coefficient of thermal expansion is 1.0 × 10−5 per degree.


Analysis
The transient heat transfer problem is analyzed in Abaqus/Standard using a heat transfer procedure for a time period of 6 seconds, so the structure is allowed to come to thermal equilibrium. The integration procedure used in Abaqus/Standard for transient heat transfer analysis introduces a relationship between the minimum usable time increment and the element size and material properties. The guideline given in Uncoupled Heat Transfer Analysis is

Δ
t
>
ρ
c
6
k
Δ
l
2
,
where 
Δ
l
 is the size of the smallest element in the mesh. If time increments smaller than this value are used, spurious oscillations may appear in the solution. Since the mesh is rather coarse, the minimum usable time increment predicted by the above formula is 4.17 × 10−4 seconds. A suggested initial time increment of 5 × 10−4 seconds is, therefore, used.

Automatic time incrementation is chosen by setting a value for the maximum temperature change allowed in an increment during a heat transfer analysis. Smaller values for the maximum temperature change cannot be used in this problem because they result in time increments that are smaller than the minimum usable time increment described above. As a consequence, the thermal analysis is rather approximate. A finer mesh would be necessary to obtain more accurate results.

The stress analysis uses the temperature distribution obtained in the heat transfer analysis to define the thermal loading. The quasi-static procedure (Quasi-Static Analysis) is used with automatic incrementation, chosen by specifying a value for the maximum difference in the creep strain increment over a time increment. This value is set to 2.0 × 10−3, which is of the same order of magnitude as the maximum elastic strain. The time period is 6 seconds, and the initial suggested time increment is 5.0 × 10−4 seconds to capture the high temperature gradients that occur very early in the analysis.

In Abaqus/Explicit the thermal and mechanical responses of the slab are determined simultaneously. The automatic time incrementation scheme available in Abaqus/Explicit is used to ensure numerical stability and to advance the solution in time.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Beam/gap example
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: beam_under_flexural_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
The system consists of three parallel cantilever beams arranged vertically with small initial gaps between them at five discrete locations along their length. Each beam has a total length of 50 units and is modeled using five cubic beam elements of type B23. The beams are linear elastic with Young’s modulus 
𝐸 = 10^8. The cross-section is a hexagonal tube with a circumscribing radius of 0.5 and a wall thickness of 0.1. Units are consistent but not intended to represent a physical system.

Initially, all five gap locations are open with a clearance of 0.01. The structural behavior is linear in bending, and only small displacements are considered. The overall nonlinearity of the problem arises solely from the opening and closing of contact gaps as the load increases.

Boundary Conditions

All three beams are completely fixed at their left ends, forming cantilever supports. At this fixed end, no movement or rotation is allowed, meaning there is no horizontal displacement, no vertical displacement, and no rotation. Along the rest of their lengths, the beams are free to deform under loading, except at the five designated gap locations where contact interaction may occur if the beams come into contact.

Loading

A pair of pinching loads is applied at the midspan (25 units from the fixed end):
A downward concentrated load 𝑃 at the midpoint of the top beam.mAn upward concentrated load 𝑃 at the midpoint of the bottom beam. The middle beam is not directly loaded and responds only through contact forces. The load magnitude increases monotonically from 0 to 200 and is applied in 10 equal increments during the static analysis.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Composite shells in cylindrical bending
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: shell_curved_plate
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This example verifies the transverse shear stress calculations in Abaqus for multilayer composite shells and demonstrates the use of the plane stress orthotropic failure measures. A discussion of the transverse shear stresses obtained by composite solids in Abaqus/Standard is included in this example. The problem consists of a two- or three-layer plate subjected to a sinusoidal distributed load, as described by Pagano (1969). The resulting transverse shear and axial stresses through the thickness of the plate are compared to two existing analytical solutions by Pagano (1969). The first solution is derived from classical laminated plate theory (CPT), while the second is an exact solution from linear elasticity theory.

The model consists of a laminated composite plate of span length 𝑙 and total thickness ℎ, subjected to a spatially varying transverse distributed load. The plate is made of orthotropic fiber-reinforced layers of equal thickness. Each layer represents a unidirectional composite material with different elastic properties in the longitudinal (L, fiber direction) and transverse (T) directions. Each layer models a fiber/matrix composite with the following properties:

E
L
172.4 GPa (25 × 106 lb/in2)
E
T
6.90 GPa (1.0 × 106 lb/in2)
G
L
T
3.45 GPa (0.5 × 106 lb/in2)
G
T
T
1.38 GPa (0.2 × 106 lb/in2)
ν
L
T
=
ν
T
T
0.25
where L signifies the direction parallel to the fibers and T signifies the transverse direction. In Abaqus/Standard two methods are used to specify the lay-up definition for the conventional shell element model. First, a composite shell section is defined to specify the thickness, number of integration points, material name, and orientation of each layer. Second, a composite general shell section is defined to specify the thickness, material name, and angle of orientation relative to the section orientation (the default shell directions in this case) for each layer. In Abaqus/Explicit only the former method is used. The material properties are specified using the orthotropic elastic in plane stress definition. The orientation of the fibers in each layer is defined by an in-plane rotation angle measured relative to the local shell directions or relative to an orientation definition given for the general shell section.

In addition to the methods outlined above, a third method of stacking continuum shell elements is used to specify the lay-up definition for a composite model. This method can be used effectively to study localized behavior, since continuum shell elements handle high aspect ratios between the in-plane dimension and the thickness dimension well.

The lay-up definition for the continuum (solid) element model in Abaqus/Standard is specified using a composite solid section definition. The thickness, material name, and orientation definition are specified for each layer.

Boundary Conditions

The plate is simply supported at both ends:

Vertical displacement is constrained at x=0 and x=l. Rotations are free, consistent with classical simple support conditions. The longitudinal edges are constrained to impose plane strain in the y-direction. No in-plane constraints are imposed along the top surface. A distributed load with a sinusoidal distribution in space, 
p=p0sin(πx/l), is applied to the top of the composite plate. In Abaqus/Standard the load is applied using user subroutine DLOAD in a static linear analysis step. In addition, an Abaqus/Standard input file is included that demonstrates the use of the DCOUP3D element to apply this distributed load. In Abaqus/Explicit the load is applied instantaneously at time 
t=0.

Two composite plates are analyzed in this example. The first is a two-layer plate with the fibers oriented parallel and orthogonal to the x-axis in the bottom and top layer, respectively. In the second plate, which has three layers of equal thickness, the fibers in the outer layers are oriented parallel to the x-axis, while the fibers in the middle layer are orthogonal to the x-axis. The span-to-thickness ratio of the plates, 
s=l/h, is varied from 4 to 30 in the Abaqus/Standard analysis; in Abaqus/Explicit this ratio is 4 throughout the analysis.

A 1 × 10 mesh of second-order S8R shell elements is used to model the plates in Abaqus/Standard. A 2 × 10 mesh of first-order S4R shell elements is used to model the plates in Abaqus/Explicit. The S4R, S8R, and S8RT shell elements are well-suited for modeling thick composite shells since they account for transverse shear flexibility. Five integration points are specified through the thickness of each layer with the models that use the shell section. This provides sufficient data to describe the stress distributions through the thickness of each layer. For the models that use the general shell section, only three points are available for output. (Since the analysis is linear elastic, three points are sufficient to determine all fields through the thickness.) The plate with the lowest span-to-thickness ratio is also analyzed with Abaqus/Standard using a 1 × 10 mesh of second-order C3D20R composite solid elements.

To illustrate the stacking capability of continuum shell elements, several meshes are provided for the two- and three-layer plates with a span-to-thickness ratio of 4. The two-layer plate is modeled with a 2 × 10 mesh of SC8R elements, each element representing a single layer of the 90/0 composite plate. One model of the three-layer plate uses a 1 × 10 mesh of SC8R elements using a single element through the thickness with a composite section definition. Another model of the three-layer plate uses a 3 × 10 mesh of SC8R elements, each element representing a single layer of the 0/90/0 composite plate. Additional models of the three-layer plate with 6, 12, and 24 elements through the thickness are provided. In these models each composite layer is modeled with 2, 4, and 8 elements through the thickness, respectively.

Additional input files using SC8R elements are included to illustrate defining the stacking and thickness direction independent of the element nodal connectivity.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Thick composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure using two radial solid elements 
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This example provides verification of composite solid continuum elements in Abaqus. The problem consists of an infinitely long composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure under plane strain conditions. The solution is compared with the analytical solution of Lekhnitskii and with finite element models using different through-thickness discretizations.

The inside radius is 60 mm and the outside radius is 140 mm. The structure consists of eight orthotropic layers of equal thickness arranged in a stacking sequence of [0°, 90°]4. The laminae are stacked in the radial direction, with fibers oriented along the circumferential and axial directions. A 0° rotation corresponds to fibers aligned with the circumferential direction.

The orthotropic elastic properties are defined using engineering constants for two materials representing circumferential and axial fiber orientations. Three section integration points are specified in each layer.

Because of symmetry, only a quarter segment of the cylinder is modeled. The model is discretized with four elements in the circumferential direction, one element in the axial direction, and two quadratic solid elements in the radial direction. A nonuniform mesh is used, with two material layers assigned to the inner radial element and six layers assigned to the outer radial element to capture the nonlinear variation of radial displacement through the thickness.

The model is constrained in the axial direction to impose plane strain conditions. A constant internal pressure of 50 MPa is applied in a linear perturbation static step.

Geometry description
A thick hollow cylinder is defined with a geometry that is axisymmetric about the cylinder axis. A uniform internal pressure p is applied along the inner surface.

The cylinder wall consists of eight concentric composite laminas stacked through the thickness. The layup alternates between 0 degree and 90 degree fiber orientations, starting with a 0 degree ply at the inner surface and ending with a 90 degree ply at the outer surface. The total wall thickness is denoted by t.

A centerline is indicated for the axisymmetric representation.
</problem_description>

case name: Thick composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure using one radial solid element with eight composite plies

<problem_description>
This example provides verification of composite solid continuum elements in Abaqus. The problem consists of an infinitely long composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure under plane strain conditions. The solution is compared with the analytical solution of Lekhnitskii and with finite element models using different through-thickness discretizations.

The inside radius is 60 mm and the outside radius is 140 mm. The structure consists of eight orthotropic layers of equal thickness arranged in a stacking sequence of [0°, 90°]4. The laminae are stacked in the radial direction.

The orthotropic elastic properties are defined using engineering constants. Three section integration points are specified in each layer.

Because of symmetry, only a quarter segment of the cylinder is modeled. The model is discretized with four elements in the circumferential direction, one element in the axial direction, and a single quadratic solid element in the radial direction. All eight plies are defined explicitly within one composite solid section by specifying alternating 0° and 90° fiber orientations.

The model is constrained in the axial direction to impose plane strain conditions. A constant internal pressure of 50 MPa is applied in a linear perturbation static step.

Geometry description
A thick hollow cylinder is defined with a geometry that is axisymmetric about the cylinder axis. A uniform internal pressure p is applied along the inner surface.

The cylinder wall consists of eight concentric composite laminas stacked through the thickness. The layup alternates between 0 degree and 90 degree fiber orientations, starting with a 0 degree ply at the inner surface and ending with a 90 degree ply at the outer surface. The total wall thickness is denoted by t.

A centerline is indicated for the axisymmetric representation.

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Thick composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure using ply-wise radial element discretization
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: composite
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This example provides verification of composite solid continuum elements in Abaqus. The problem consists of an infinitely long composite cylinder subjected to internal pressure under plane strain conditions.

The inside radius is 60 mm and the outside radius is 140 mm. The structure consists of eight orthotropic layers of equal thickness arranged in a stacking sequence of [0°, 90°]4.

The orthotropic elastic properties are defined using engineering constants for circumferential and axial fiber orientations. In this model, the finite element mesh is partitioned into element sets corresponding to circumferential and axial fiber-dominated regions. Separate composite solid section definitions are assigned to these element sets to represent the stacking sequence.

Because of symmetry, only a quarter segment of the cylinder is modeled. The model is discretized with quadratic solid elements in the circumferential, radial, and axial directions.

The model is constrained in the axial direction to impose plane strain conditions. A constant internal pressure of 50 MPa is applied in a linear perturbation static step.

Geometry description
A thick hollow cylinder is defined with a geometry that is axisymmetric about the cylinder axis. A uniform internal pressure p is applied along the inner surface.

The cylinder wall consists of eight concentric composite laminas stacked through the thickness. The layup alternates between 0 degree and 90 degree fiber orientations, starting with a 0 degree ply at the inner surface and ending with a 90 degree ply at the outer surface. The total wall thickness is denoted by t.

A centerline is indicated for the axisymmetric representation.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Snap-through of a shallow, cylindrical roof under a point load using Modified Riks Method
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: shell_curved_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This example illustrates the use of the modified Riks method to obtain the unstable static equilibrium response of an elastic shell structure that exhibits snap-through behavior. The shell is a shallow cylindrical roof pinned along its straight edges and loaded by a point load at its midpoint. Comparison with published results provides verification of this type of analysis.

The dimensions of the roof are shown in Figure 1. The material is linear elastic with a Young’s modulus of 3.103 GPa and a Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

The roof is assumed to deform symmetrically, so one quadrant is discretized using a regular 6 × 6 mesh of S4R5 shell elements with Gauss section integration using five section points.

Geometric nonlinearity is included. The unstable equilibrium path is traced using the modified Riks method. An initial load increment corresponding to a total applied load of 3000 N is specified. The analysis is terminated when the load proportionality factor reaches 0.06, corresponding to a total applied load of approximately 720 N. The modified Riks algorithm allows the solution to follow load reversals that occur during snap-through.

Model description
A shallow cylindrical shell roof is modeled using a quarter-symmetry representation. The shell has a cylindrical curvature with radius 2.54 m, a span length of 254 mm in each planar direction of the modeled quadrant, and a uniform thickness of 6.35 mm.

Two opposite curved edges are pinned, while the other two edges are free. The figure indicates that only one quadrant of the full roof is modeled.

A concentrated vertical load is applied at the center of the roof surface. A global coordinate system is shown, and the geometric parameters include the curvature radius, in-plane span, and thickness.

</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Snap-through of a shallow, cylindrical roof under a point load using Automatic Stabilization
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: shell_curved_plate
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>

This example illustrates the use of automatic stabilization to obtain the unstable static response of an elastic shell structure exhibiting snap-through behavior. The shell is a shallow cylindrical roof pinned along its straight edges and loaded by a point load at its midpoint.

The dimensions of the roof are shown in Figure 1. The material is linear elastic with a Young’s modulus of 3.103 GPa and a Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

The roof is assumed to deform symmetrically, so one quadrant is discretized using a regular 6 × 6 mesh of S4R5 shell elements with Gauss section integration using five section points.

Geometric nonlinearity is included. Instead of using the modified Riks method, automatic stabilization with volume proportional damping is employed. A total load of 1332 N is applied with an initial increment equal to 10 percent of the total load. This procedure does not capture load reversals explicitly; during the unstable portion of the deformation, viscous forces generated by damping balance the externally applied load, resulting in an approximately constant load during snap-through.

Model description
A shallow cylindrical shell roof is modeled using a quarter-symmetry representation. The shell has a cylindrical curvature with radius 2.54 m, a span length of 254 mm in each planar direction of the modeled quadrant, and a uniform thickness of 6.35 mm.

Two opposite curved edges are pinned, while the other two edges are free. The figure indicates that only one quadrant of the full roof is modeled.

A concentrated vertical load is applied at the center of the roof surface. A global coordinate system is shown, and the geometric parameters include the curvature radius, in-plane span, and thickness.

</problem_description>

case name: Pressurized rubber disc using Explicit (dynamic)
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: polymer 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the thick rubber disc using shell elements in Abaqus Explicit.

The disc has a radius of 7.5 in and is modeled as a shell with a thickness of 0.5 defined in the shell section. The material is hyperelastic with polynomial strain energy constants C10 = 80 and C01 = 20. A density of 1.0E-4 is included for explicit dynamics.

The mesh uses S4R reduced integration shell elements with cylindrical orientation. Symmetry boundary conditions are applied along the appropriate edges, and the outer boundary is modeled as pinned.

A dynamic explicit analysis is performed over a total time of 0.01. A uniform pressure of 46 is applied to the shell surface using element set SHEET and a linear ramp amplitude. The response captures large membrane stretching behavior under pressure, including dynamic effects inherent to the explicit procedure.

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Pressurized rubber disc with Standard (implicit, Riks)
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: polymer
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes a thick rubber disc subjected to uniform pressure using an axisymmetric continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The disc is pinned along its outer edge and undergoes large deformation as it bulges outward under pressure.

The disc has a radius of 7.5 in and is modeled with a thickness of 0.25 in in the axisymmetric domain. The material is modeled as an incompressible hyperelastic material using a first order polynomial strain energy function with constants C10 = 80 and C01 = 20.

The mesh uses CAX4IH hybrid axisymmetric continuum elements, which are suitable for nearly incompressible behavior. The pinned outer edge is enforced using equation constraints that keep the boundary straight while allowing rotation about the pinned point.

A geometrically nonlinear static analysis is performed using the modified Riks method. The unsymmetric equation solver is activated because pressure loading with the pinned edge treatment introduces nonsymmetric stiffness terms. A uniform pressure of 200 is applied to the bottom surface of the disc using element set BOTEL and load type P1. The Riks parameters specify an initial increment of 0.01 and allow tracing of the nonlinear equilibrium path through large deformation.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Stretching of a plate with a central circular hole under uniaxial loading (open hole tension)
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category: flat_plate
case material: polymer 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the large deformation response of a thin elastic sheet containing a centrally located circular hole subjected to uniaxial stretching. Plane stress conditions are assumed.

The undeformed square sheet has a thickness of 0.079 in and a side length corresponding to 6.5 in in the full model. A quarter of the sheet is modeled using symmetry about the x = 0 and y = 0 planes. The circular hole is located at the center of the full sheet and is represented in the quarter model by curved boundary geometry generated through circular node generation.

The mesh consists of 32 second order reduced integration plane stress elements of type CPS8R. The element distribution is biased toward the hole using a grading factor to better capture the stress concentration in the region of highest strain gradients.

The material behavior is defined using the Ogden hyperelastic formulation with N = 3. Instead of specifying material constants directly, the TEST DATA INPUT option is used. Experimental data from Treloar are provided in the form of uniaxial, biaxial, and planar test data. Abaqus internally determines the Ogden parameters that best fit the supplied test data. The material is assumed to be incompressible in plane stress, with thickness change accommodating volume preservation.

Boundary conditions enforce symmetry along the left and bottom edges of the quarter model. The top and bottom edges are restrained in the y direction to prevent vertical stretch, producing uniaxial deformation in the x direction. A uniform horizontal displacement is prescribed on the right edge by constraining all nodes on that edge to have the same x displacement using an equation constraint. The retained node on that edge, node 1601, is prescribed a final displacement of 20.0 units in the x direction. The total stretching force is obtained from the reaction at this node.

A geometrically nonlinear static analysis is performed with automatic incrementation. The initial increment size is 0.05, and large strain effects are included through NLGEOM. Stresses, strains, reaction forces, and strain energy are monitored during loading to evaluate the large deformation response and stress concentration around the hole.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index> 
case name: Necking of a round tensile bar
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category: solid_column_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the necking behavior of a round tensile bar using an axisymmetric finite element model. The specimen has an initial radius R0 equal to 1 and a half length l0 such that l0 over R0 equals 4. Because of symmetry about the radial axis r = 0 and the mid plane z = 0, only one quarter of the specimen is modeled.

The geometry and deformation are assumed to be axisymmetric. The mesh is constructed using 4 node bilinear axisymmetric reduced integration elements of type CAX4R. The mesh is refined toward the center of the bar, where necking and strain localization are expected to occur. A geometric bias is used in the axial direction to concentrate elements in the region of highest deformation.

The material is modeled as an elastic plastic metal with porous metal plasticity to capture void growth and ductile softening. The elastic properties are Youngs modulus E = 300 and Poissons ratio nu = 0.3. The plastic behavior is defined by a tabulated yield stress versus equivalent plastic strain curve corresponding to a power law type hardening response with initial yield stress equal to 1.0 and hardening exponent N approximately equal to 0.1.

Porous metal plasticity is included with parameters q1 = 1.5, q2 = 1.0, and q3 = 2.25. The initial relative density is 1.0, corresponding to an initial void volume fraction f0 = 0. Void nucleation is defined by a normal distribution in equivalent plastic strain with mean strain 0.3, standard deviation 0.1, and total nucleated void volume fraction 0.04. This formulation allows progressive void growth and softening leading to localization and neck formation.

Symmetry boundary conditions are applied along r = 0 so that radial displacement is zero, and along z = 0 so that axial displacement is zero. The nodes on the top surface at z = 4.0 are constrained in the radial direction and are subjected to prescribed axial displacement. The loading is applied in two static general steps with geometric nonlinearity enabled. In the first step the top surface is displaced in the axial direction to 0.76. In the second step the displacement is increased further to 0.79 to continue the deformation into the necking regime.

Automatic time incrementation is used in each step, with an initial increment size of 0.001 and a maximum time period specified to control the solution. Reaction forces and displacements at the top surface are monitored to evaluate the load versus displacement response and to capture the onset and progression of necking driven by void growth and plastic softening.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Concrete slump test 
case domain: dynamic_analysis_not_vibration_analysis
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: concrete 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case simulates a concrete slump test using an axisymmetric finite element model. A conical concrete specimen is allowed to deform under its own weight after removal of the supporting mold. The analysis accounts for finite strains and large displacements.

The cone has an initial height of 0.3 units, a base radius of 0.1, and a top radius of 0.05. Because the geometry and loading are axisymmetric, a two dimensional axisymmetric model is used. The mesh consists of first order four node axisymmetric elements of type CAX4. The domain is discretized with 10 elements along the height and 5 elements along the radial direction.

The material is modeled using an elastic plastic cast iron plasticity formulation. The elastic properties are Youngs modulus E = 2.25 and Poissons ratio nu = 0.125. A density of 0.1 is defined to represent self weight loading. The cast iron plasticity model includes different hardening responses in tension and compression. A tension hardening parameter of 3.173E-03 at zero plastic strain and a compression hardening parameter of 5.0E-03 at zero plastic strain are specified. The model captures pressure dependent yielding and different strengths in tension and compression.

Boundary conditions enforce axisymmetry by constraining radial displacement along the centerline r = 0. The base of the cone is restrained in the vertical direction but is free to move radially, so friction with the support is neglected.

The loading consists of a gravity body force applied to the entire model, with magnitude 0.6666 acting in the negative vertical direction. The load is applied in a static general step with geometric nonlinearity enabled. The gravity load is increased gradually from zero to its full value over the step. The unsymmetric solver is activated to improve convergence for the pressure dependent plasticity formulation. Field equation tolerances are adjusted to improve computational efficiency.

The vertical displacement of a node at the top of the cone is monitored to evaluate the slump response. Stresses, plastic strains, and reaction forces at the base are recorded to assess the inelastic deformation and final deformed shape of the concrete specimen under self weight.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: The Hertz contact problem using 2D Plane Strain Model
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models the classic Hertz contact problem using a two dimensional plane strain approximation. Two identical infinitely long cylinders pressed together can be represented by a deformable quarter cylinder contacting a flat rigid surface because of symmetry. Material behavior is linear elastic and geometric nonlinearity is turned off, so the only nonlinearity comes from contact.

Geometry and model setup are built as a quarter of the cylinder cross section. The deformable cylinder is meshed with plane strain reduced integration elements CPE4R. A rigid line (R2D2) represents the flat rigid surface. A reference node is defined for the rigid body to collect reactions.

Boundary conditions enforce symmetry by fixing horizontal displacement along the left symmetry plane of the quarter cylinder. The top boundary of the deformable cylinder is displacement controlled in the vertical direction to press the cylinder into the rigid surface. The motion is applied with a smooth step amplitude so the loading ramps up gradually. The prescribed vertical displacement is -0.4 over a step time of 0.011.

Contact is defined between the bottom surface of the deformable body and the rigid surface. The interaction is frictionless. Contact output is requested to capture contact stresses and contact forces, and reaction forces are recorded at the rigid body reference node to obtain the total load per unit thickness.

Solver and procedure

The analysis is run in Abaqus Explicit using dynamic explicit time integration. Even though it is an explicit dynamic step, the loading is ramped smoothly to achieve a quasi static response for contact. Density is provided to support the explicit procedure.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: The Hertz contact problem using 3D Solid Model
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: axisymmetric_solid
case material: metal  
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models the Hertz contact problem in three dimensions using a unit thickness cylinder segment with plane strain enforced through the thickness. Two identical infinitely long cylinders pressed together are represented as a deformable quarter cylinder pressed against a flat rigid surface. Material behavior is linear elastic and geometric nonlinearity is turned off, so contact is the only source of nonlinearity.

The deformable body is a three dimensional solid mesh created by extruding the two dimensional quarter cylinder cross section to a thickness of 1.0. The cylinder is meshed with reduced integration brick elements C3D8R. Plane strain conditions are imposed by constraining the out of plane displacement on the two exterior faces of the model (front and back). A rigid surface is modeled with rigid quadrilateral elements R3D4, tied to a rigid body reference node.

Boundary conditions enforce symmetry and remove rigid body motion. Horizontal displacement is fixed along the left symmetry plane of the deformable cylinder. The rigid body reference node is constrained in all degrees of freedom so the rigid surface stays fixed. Out of plane displacement is fixed on the front and back faces to enforce plane strain. The top surface of the deformable cylinder is displaced downward using a smooth step amplitude. The prescribed vertical displacement is -0.4 over a step time of 0.011.

Contact is modeled using general contact with an assigned frictionless contact property. Contact is applied to all exterior surfaces, allowing the deformable cylinder to interact with the rigid surface during the indentation.

Solver and procedure

The analysis is run in Abaqus Explicit using dynamic explicit integration. The displacement loading is ramped smoothly to reduce inertial effects and approximate quasi static Hertz contact conditions. Reaction forces at the rigid body reference node can be used to obtain the total applied load, and displacement history is recorded for selected nodes near the contact region.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Pipe crushing under compression
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_compression
case category: hollow_column_under_axial_loading
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case models the crushing of a long, straight pipe section between a rigid, flat anvil using a two-dimensional plane strain formulation in Abaqus/Standard. Only one quadrant of the pipe cross-section is modeled by exploiting symmetry about the horizontal and vertical axes.

The pipe is discretized using CPE8H elements, which are 8-node, fully integrated, hybrid plane strain elements. The mesh represents a quarter of the circular section with two elements through the thickness and multiple elements around the circumference. A solid section is assigned with an elastic-plastic material model. The material behavior consists of linear elasticity followed by isotropic hardening plasticity defined by tabulated stress–plastic strain data.

The outer surface of the pipe is defined as a contact surface. The rigid anvil is modeled as an analytical rigid surface defined by line segments and assigned a rigid body constraint with a reference node. Contact between the pipe and the anvil is defined using a surface-to-surface contact pair with a frictionless surface interaction.

Symmetry boundary conditions are applied along the two cut planes of the quadrant model using XSYMM and YSYMM constraints. Crushing is imposed by prescribing a downward vertical displacement of -1.3 at the rigid body reference node. The horizontal displacement and rotation of the rigid body reference node are constrained to prevent rigid body motion.

The analysis is performed using a Static, General step with large-deformation effects enabled (NLGEOM). The objective of the simulation is to obtain the load-displacement response of the crushed pipe section and to capture the associated large plastic deformations under frictionless contact with the rigid anvil.

Geometry
A straight circular pipe segment is modeled with a hollow cylindrical cross-section. The pipe has an outside diameter of 114.3 mm (4.5 in), a wall thickness of 8.87 mm (0.349 in), and a length of 25.4 mm (1.0 in).

The pipe segment is shown positioned between two rigid, flat plates representing compression platens. The plates are parallel, and the pipe axis is oriented parallel to the plate surfaces, indicating diametral crushing of the pipe segment between the platens.
</problem_description>
<input_file>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Uniformly loaded elastic-plastic plate
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the quasi-static stretching of a square plate with a circular hole using Abaqus/Explicit only. The geometry consists of a 30 by 30 plate with a hole of radius 4. A quarter-symmetry model is used. The input file contains three identical quarter meshes placed side by side, each associated with a different plasticity definition.

All meshes are discretized using CPS4R elements, which are 4-node plane stress, reduced integration elements with enhanced hourglass control. A solid section with enhanced hourglass control is assigned to each mesh.

The elastic properties are Young’s modulus 1.0e9 and Poisson’s ratio 0.3. The density is 2500. Plastic behavior is defined with isotropic hardening using a two-point stress–plastic strain curve with an initial yield of 1.0e6 and hardening to 5.0e6 at a plastic strain of 10.0. Three material definitions are used. The first uses isotropic plasticity. The second and third use anisotropic plasticity defined through a potential, with coefficients of 1.5 and 0.66667 in the x-direction, respectively. For the anisotropic cases, a material orientation aligned with the global coordinate system is specified.

Symmetry boundary conditions are applied along the two symmetry edges of each quarter model, enforcing zero displacement normal to each symmetry plane. Along the outer vertical boundary, horizontal displacement is restrained. The plate is stretched in the y-direction by prescribing a vertical velocity of 5.0 at the top edge. The velocity is ramped from zero to full value during the first half of the step time and then maintained constant for the remainder of the analysis using a defined amplitude.

The analysis is performed in a single Dynamic, Explicit step with a total time of 1.0. Bulk viscosity parameters are included for numerical damping. The objective of the simulation is to compare deformation patterns and equivalent plastic strain development around the hole for isotropic and anisotropic plasticity under explicit quasi-static stretching.
</problem_description>
