<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Simply supported solid 3D plate under concentrated central loading
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model simulates the bending response of a square solid plate subjected to concentrated loading at the center of its top surface. The case represents a classical plate bending problem where the plate is simply supported along its edges and loaded by a distributed transverse pressure acting on the top surface. The objective of the model is to compute the displacement and stress distribution in the plate under static loading while demonstrating a structured mesh generation strategy using Abaqus input file commands.

The plate has in plane dimensions of 100 mm by 100 mm and a thickness of 5 mm. The plate is modeled as a three dimensional solid extending from z = -2.5 mm to z = +2.5 mm. The analysis is performed in Abaqus Standard using a linear static step with geometric nonlinearity disabled. The material is modeled as linear elastic and isotropic.

A structured hexahedral mesh is generated entirely using Abaqus keyword commands rather than explicitly listing nodes and elements. The mesh uses C3D8R elements, which are eight node linear brick elements with reduced integration. The plate is discretized using 8 elements along the x direction, 8 elements along the y direction, and 3 elements through the thickness.

Node generation begins by defining the corner nodes of the bottom and top surfaces of the plate. Edge nodes are generated using the Abaqus command NGEN, which creates evenly spaced nodes between two defined nodes. Once the edge nodes are created, the Abaqus command NFILL is used to generate the interior nodes of the bottom and top surfaces, producing structured node grids on both faces. A second NFILL operation then generates intermediate nodes between the bottom and top surfaces, creating the layered node structure through the plate thickness.

Element generation is performed using a single seed element and the Abaqus command ELGEN. The seed element is defined using the nodes of the lower left corner of the mesh, and ELGEN is then used to replicate this element pattern in the x direction, y direction, and through the thickness direction. This generates the full structured mesh using a compact set of commands.


Because the structured mesh contains an even number of elements in the in plane directions, there is no node located exactly at the geometric center of the plate. As a result, a true point load cannot be applied directly at the center node.To approximate a concentrated central load, a small surface patch located around the plate center is used. The element numbering pattern generated by ELGEN is used to identify the elements located near the center of the top surface. In the 8 by 8 top layer mesh, the plate center lies at the intersection of four neighboring elements. These four elements form a symmetric region surrounding the geometric center of the plate. They are collected into a dedicated element set representing the central loading region. A surface definition is then created using these elements and the element face corresponding to the top surface. For the C3D8R element, the face labeled S2 corresponds to nodes five through eight of each element, which lie on the top surface of the plate. A distributed load is applied to this small surface patch to approximate a concentrated center load. Simply supported conditions are approximated by constraining the transverse displacement U3 along the edge lines of the bottom surface of the plate. The resulting solution produces the characteristic plate bending response with maximum deflection near the plate center.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Modal analysis of a simply supported 3D solid plate
case domain: vibrationanalysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model performs a modal analysis of a square solid plate using three dimensional continuum elements. The objective of the analysis is to compute the natural frequencies of the structure using a structured hexahedral mesh generated entirely through Abaqus keyword commands.

The plate has in plane dimensions of 100 mm by 100 mm and a thickness of 5 mm. The bottom surface lies at z = -2.5 mm and the top surface lies at z = 2.5 mm. The model therefore represents a solid plate centered about the mid thickness plane.

Structured mesh construction strategy

The mesh is constructed using a structured grid on the bottom and top surfaces, followed by element generation using a single seed element. The bottom and top surfaces each contain a 21 by 21 node grid, which produces a 20 by 20 element mesh in the plane of the plate. Only one element is used through the thickness.

Node generation strategy

Four corner nodes are first defined on the bottom surface of the plate and four corresponding corner nodes are defined on the top surface. The bottom surface corner nodes define the square plate boundary at z = -2.5 mm and the top surface corner nodes define the corresponding points at z = 2.5 mm.

Nodes along the bottom and top edges in the x direction are generated using the Abaqus command NGEN. This creates the full node rows between the corner nodes on each surface. The node numbering increases sequentially along each row.

Intermediate node rows between the bottom and top edges of each surface are then generated using the Abaqus command NFILL. This creates the structured grid of nodes across the plate surface. The node numbering scheme uses an increment of 100 between successive rows so that each row of nodes is easily identifiable and structured.

Element generation

A single eight node brick element is defined between the first four nodes on the bottom surface and the corresponding nodes on the top surface. This seed element connects the bottom node row to the corresponding top node row.

The Abaqus command ELGEN is then used to replicate this seed element to form the full structured mesh. The element generation produces 20 elements along the x direction and 20 elements along the y direction, resulting in a total of 400 C3D8R elements. Since only one element is used through the thickness, the plate is represented by a single layer of solid elements between the bottom and top node grids.

Material properties

The plate material is modeled as a linear elastic isotropic solid with Young's modulus equal to 200000 MPa, Poisson's ratio equal to 0.3, and density equal to 7.8e-09 in the chosen unit system.

Analysis procedure

The natural frequencies of the plate are computed using a frequency extraction step with the Lanczos eigensolver. Six eigenvalues are requested in order to obtain the first six vibration modes of the plate.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:Clamped Plate subjected to pressure loading  
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending 
case category:flat_plate 
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the bending response of a square plate subjected to a uniformly distributed pressure load using Abaqus Standard.
The plate has dimensions 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements lying in the global XY plane. The thickness is defined through a shell section assigned to all elements. A structured mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined first, and intermediate nodes are created along the bottom and top edges using NGEN. The interior node grid is then generated using NFILL to form a uniform 20 by 20 mesh. A single quadrilateral shell element is defined and replicated across the domain using ELGEN, resulting in a fully structured mesh.
The material is modeled as linear elastic with Young's modulus 200000 MPa and Poisson's ratio 0.3.
The plate is fully clamped along all four edges. This is implemented by constraining degrees of freedom 1 through 5 on the left, right, top, and bottom edge node sets. This removes all in-plane translations, out-of-plane displacement, and rotational degrees of freedom along the boundaries, enforcing a fully fixed edge condition.
A uniformly distributed pressure load is applied over the entire plate surface using DLOAD on the full element set. The pressure acts normal to the plate surface and produces bending deformation.
The analysis is performed using a static step with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the bending response of a fully clamped plate under uniform pressure loading and observe the resulting displacement and stress distribution across the plate.
</problem_description>

<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the natural vibration characteristics of a square plate using a modal analysis in Abaqus Standard.
The plate has dimensions 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements lying in the global XY plane. The thickness is defined through a shell section assigned to all elements. A structured mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined first, and intermediate nodes are created along the bottom and top edges using NGEN. The interior node grid is then generated using NFILL to form a uniform 20 by 20 mesh. The plate is fully clamped along all four edges. This is implemented by constraining degrees of freedom 1 through 5 on the left, right, top, and bottom edge node sets. This removes all translational and rotational degrees of freedom along the boundaries, enforcing a fully fixed edge condition.
A frequency extraction step is used with a perturbation procedure. The Lanczos eigensolver is employed to compute the natural frequencies and corresponding mode shapes of the structure. Six modes are requested, and mass normalization is used for the eigenvectors.
The objective of the simulation is to determine the natural frequencies and associated mode shapes of a fully clamped plate and to observe the characteristic vibration patterns under these boundary conditions.

<index>
case name:PLATE CLAMPED ON BOTTOM FOUR EDGES AND SUBJECT TO CONCENTRATED LOADING ON TOP SURFACE  
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending 
case category:flat_plate 
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the bending response of a clamped square plate subjected to a concentrated central load using shell elements in Abaqus Standard.

The plate has in-plane dimensions of 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled as a full geometry in the global XY plane. The thickness is defined through a shell section assigned to all elements.

The mesh is generated as a structured 20 by 20 grid using S4R shell elements. Nodes are first defined at the four plate corners, then NGEN is used to create nodes along the bottom and top edges. NFILL is used to interpolate nodes between these edges to form the full midsurface grid. A single seed element is defined and replicated across the plate using ELGEN to obtain a uniform mesh.

The material is modeled as linear elastic with Young's modulus 200000 MPa and Poisson's ratio 0.3.

Clamped boundary conditions are applied along all four edges by constraining translational and rotational degrees of freedom at the edges, enforcing U1 = U2 = U3 = U4 = U5 = 0.

A concentrated central load is approximated by applying a high pressure over a small patch of elements located at the plate center. For the 20 by 20 structured mesh, the geometric center lies between elements, so a symmetric 2 by 2 element patch around the center is selected using the element set CENTERPATCH. A pressure load is applied to this patch using DLOAD to represent a concentrated load in a numerically stable manner.

The analysis is performed using a static step with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the localized bending response and stress distribution of the plate under a concentrated central load.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name: Simply supported composite plate under uniform pressure loading  
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: flat_plate
case material: composite 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the bending response of a simply supported square composite plate subjected to uniform transverse pressure using shell elements in Abaqus Standard.
The plate has in plane dimensions of 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled as a full geometry in the global x y plane. The laminate is represented using a composite shell section with a symmetric four ply layup of 0 90 90 0. Each ply has equal thickness, giving a total laminate thickness of 1.0 mm.
The mesh is generated as a structured 20 by 20 grid using S4R shell elements. Nodes are first defined at the four plate corners, then NGEN is used to create nodes along the bottom and top edges. NFILL is used to interpolate nodes between these edges to form the full midsurface grid. A single seed shell element is defined and replicated across the plate using ELGEN to obtain a uniform mesh.
The material is defined as an orthotropic lamina using engineering constants and assigned through the composite shell section to capture the layered behavior.
Simply supported boundary conditions are applied along all four edges by constraining the transverse displacement U3 = 0, while leaving rotations free to allow bending without moment restraint.
A uniform pressure load is applied normal to the shell surface over all elements using a distributed load definition.
The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the bending response and stress distribution of the laminated composite plate under uniform loading.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: BUCKLING ANALYSIS OF SIMPLY SUPPORTED PLATE SUBJECT TO UNIAXIAL COMPRESSIVE LOADING  
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model predicts the elastic buckling behavior of a simply supported square plate subjected to uniaxial in-plane compressive loading using an eigenvalue buckling analysis in Abaqus Standard.
The plate has in-plane dimensions of 100 mm × 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements. The geometry is defined in the global X–Y plane, and the thickness is assigned through a shell section.
The mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined and intermediate nodes are created using NGEN along the bottom and top edges. NFILL is then used to generate a structured 20 × 20 mesh across the plate. A single element is defined and replicated using ELGEN to form the full mesh.
A uniform shell section with constant thickness is assigned to all elements. The material is modeled as linear elastic.
Simply supported boundary conditions are applied along all four edges by constraining the out-of-plane displacement U3 = 0. Axial displacement U1 is constrained along the left edge.
Uniaxial compressive loading is applied along the right edge (NSET=RIGHT) in the global X direction using CLOAD, while the left edge serves as the reference edge for axial restraint.
The analysis is performed using a perturbation step with the *BUCKLE procedure, which computes eigenvalues corresponding to buckling load multipliers and associated mode shapes.
The objective of the simulation is to determine the critical buckling load and corresponding buckling mode shapes of the plate under uniaxial compression.
</problem_description>

case name: BUCKLING ANALYSIS OF SIMPLY SUPPORTED PLATE SUBJECTED TO BIAXIAL COMPRESSIVE LOADING
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model predicts the elastic buckling behavior of a simply supported square plate subjected to biaxial in-plane compressive loading using an eigenvalue buckling analysis in Abaqus Standard.

The plate has in-plane dimensions of 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements. The geometry is defined in the global X Y plane, and the thickness is assigned through a shell section.

The mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined and intermediate nodes are created using NGEN along the bottom and top edges. NFILL is then used to generate a structured 20 by 20 mesh across the plate. A single element is defined and replicated using ELGEN to form the full mesh.

A uniform shell section with constant thickness is assigned to all elements. The material is modeled as linear elastic.

Simply supported boundary conditions are applied along all four edges by constraining the out-of-plane displacement U3 = 0. To establish the in-plane compression state, axial displacement U1 is constrained along the left edge and axial displacement U2 is constrained along the bottom edge.

Biaxial compressive loading is applied along the right and top edges using the CLOAD definition. Compression in the global X direction is applied to the right (NSET=RIGHT) edge, while compression in the global Y direction is applied to the top (NSET=TOP) edge.

The analysis is performed using a perturbation step with the *BUCKLE procedure, which computes eigenvalues corresponding to buckling load multipliers and associated mode shapes.

The objective of the simulation is to determine the critical buckling load and corresponding buckling mode shapes of the plate under biaxial compression.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: SIMPLY SUPPORTED PLATE SUBJECTED TO UNIAXIAL TENSILE LOADING 
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category: flat_plate
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the in-plane elastic response of a simply supported square plate subjected to uniaxial tensile loading using Abaqus Standard.

The plate has dimensions 100 mm × 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements lying in the global X–Y plane. The thickness is defined through a shell section assigned to all elements. A structured mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined and intermediate nodes are created using NGEN along the bottom and top edges, followed by NFILL to generate a uniform 20 × 20 mesh. A single quadrilateral element is defined and replicated across the domain using ELGEN.

The material is modeled as linear elastic with Young’s modulus 200000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio 0.3.

Simply supported conditions are enforced in the out-of-plane direction by constraining U3 = 0 along all four edges (LEFT, RIGHT, TOP, BOT), preventing transverse displacement while allowing in-plane deformation.

In-plane boundary conditions are applied to produce uniaxial tension. The left edge is constrained in the axial direction (U1 = 0), serving as the reference edge. A single node is additionally constrained in U2 to eliminate rigid body motion. A prescribed displacement is applied along the right edge in the global X direction (U1), generating uniform tensile deformation across the plate.

The analysis is performed using a static step. The objective of the simulation is to obtain the resulting stress distribution under uniaxial tensile loading and verify the expected uniform S11 stress field in the plate.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:SIMPLY SUPPORTED PLATE SUBJECTED TO BIAXIAL LOADING
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension  
case category:flat_plate 
case material:metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This case analyzes the in-plane elastic response of a simply supported square plate subjected to biaxial tensile loading using Abaqus Standard.

The plate has dimensions 100 mm by 100 mm and is modeled using shell elements lying in the global X Y plane. The thickness is defined through a shell section assigned to all elements. A structured mesh is generated using S4R shell elements. Corner nodes are defined and intermediate nodes are created using NGEN along the bottom and top edges, followed by NFILL to generate a uniform 20 by 20 mesh. A single quadrilateral element is defined and replicated across the domain using ELGEN.

The material is modeled as linear elastic with Young's modulus 200000 MPa and Poisson's ratio 0.3.

Simply supported conditions are enforced in the out-of-plane direction by constraining U3 = 0 along all four edges, preventing transverse displacement while allowing in-plane deformation.

In-plane boundary conditions are applied to produce uniform biaxial tension. The left edge is constrained in U1 and the bottom edge is constrained in U2 to establish the in-plane reference condition. Tensile displacement is applied along the right edge in the global X direction and along the top edge in the global Y direction. This edge-based loading and restraint pattern produces a uniform biaxial membrane stress state across the plate.

The analysis is performed using a static step. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the uniform stress distribution in the plate under biaxial tensile loading and verify the expected in-plane membrane response.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:ANNULAR SHELL DISC SIMPLY SUPPORTED ON PERIMETER UNDER UNIFORMLY DISTRIBUTED LOADING  
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending 
case category:annular 
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description
This model analyzes the bending response of an annular circular plate (disc with a central hole) using a shell formulation in Abaqus Standard. The plate has an outer radius of 10 mm, an inner radius of approximately 3.33 mm, and a uniform thickness of 2 mm. The structure lies in the global X–Y plane and is subjected to a uniformly distributed transverse load.

The geometry is modeled as a midsurface shell rather than a 3D solid. The thickness is defined analytically using a shell section, avoiding the need for through-thickness meshing. The annular geometry is discretized using a structured, sector-based topology consisting of 16 circumferential divisions and 2 radial bands, resulting in a total of 32 S4R shell elements.

The mesh generation follows a partially structured keyword-based approach. Three concentric circular node rings are defined explicitly: an inner boundary, an intermediate ring, and the outer boundary. Each ring contains 16 nodes arranged in a consistent angular sequence. This allows the annular region to be decomposed into quadrilateral sectors suitable for shell elements.

The element connectivity is generated using a hybrid strategy combining ELGEN and manual definition. A small number of seed elements are defined for one sector in each radial band. ELGEN is then used to replicate these elements circumferentially for most of the disc. However, due to the circular topology, ELGEN cannot automatically handle the wraparound from the last sector back to the first. As a result, the final sector in each radial band is defined manually to close the ring. This highlights an important limitation of ELGEN: while it works well for linear or grid-based replication, circular geometries require explicit handling of periodic connectivity.

The material is defined as linear elastic with Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3. The shell section is assigned with a thickness of 2 mm.

Boundary conditions represent a simply supported outer edge. This is implemented by constraining the transverse displacement (U3 = 0) for all nodes on the outer boundary. To prevent rigid body motion in the plane of the disc, additional constraints are applied to selected perimeter nodes, typically fixing one node in U1 and another in U2. Rotations are left free, consistent with simply supported behavior.

A uniformly distributed pressure load is applied normal to the shell surface using a DLOAD definition over the entire element set. The sign convention determines the direction of loading relative to the shell normal.

A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the stress and deformation response of an annular plate under transverse loading, while demonstrating a structured keyword-based shell modeling approach and illustrating the limitations of ELGEN when applied to circular geometries requiring wraparound connectivity.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name:ROUND SOLID DISC UNDER UNIFORMLY DISTRIBUTED LOADING AND SIMPLE SUPPORT ALONG BOTTOM PERIMETER  
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending 
case category:flat_plate
case material:metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model represents the bending response of a solid circular disc subjected to a uniformly distributed transverse pressure load using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The disc has a radius of 10 mm and a thickness of 2 mm, with its mid-plane located at Z = 0, the bottom surface at Z = -1 mm, and the top surface at Z = +1 mm. The geometry lies in the global XY-plane with thickness along the global Z-direction.

The mesh is constructed using a fully structured, keyword-based approach adapted from the solid rod topology. Each circular face is discretized into a central node, an inner ring of 8 nodes, and an outer ring of 8 nodes. This arrangement partitions the disc into 12 quadrilateral sectors, enabling a mapped hexahedral mesh. Three node layers are defined explicitly at the bottom, middle, and top surfaces. The middle layer is generated using NGEN by connecting corresponding nodes between the bottom and top faces with a node increment of 100.

The element mesh is generated by first defining 12 seed C3D8R elements between the bottom and middle layers. These seed elements are then extruded through the thickness using ELGEN, with a node increment of 100 and an element increment of 12, resulting in a total of 2 elements through the thickness and 24 structured brick elements overall. This approach ensures consistent connectivity and avoids element distortion.

The loading is applied on the top surface using an element-based surface definition. The top layer elements (elements 13 to 24) are grouped into an element set, and for the given connectivity, the loaded surface corresponds to face S1. A uniform pressure of 100 MPa is applied, acting in the negative Z-direction to produce downward bending.

The material is modeled as linear elastic with a Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and a Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

The boundary condition represents a disc supported from below along its perimeter. Only the outer-ring nodes on the bottom surface are constrained in the vertical direction by setting U3 = 0, while all other degrees of freedom remain free. This creates a discrete ring support condition that allows in-plane motion and bending while preventing vertical displacement along the supported edge.

A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The expected response is a smooth bending deformation with maximum displacement at the center of the disc and decreasing displacement toward the supported perimeter. Due to the coarse discretization using 8 sectors, the geometry appears polygonal and may introduce slight asymmetry in the displacement contours, but the overall bending behavior is correctly captured.
</problem_description>

case name:ROUND SOLID DISC UNDER CONCENTRATED CENTER LOADING AND SIMPLE SUPPORT ALONG BOTTOM PERIMETER

<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model represents the bending response of a solid circular disc subjected to a concentrated transverse load using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The disc has a radius of 10 mm and a thickness of 2 mm, with its mid-plane located at Z = 0, the bottom surface at Z = -1 mm, and the top surface at Z = +1 mm. The geometry lies in the global XY-plane with thickness along the global Z-direction.

These seed elements are then extruded through the thickness using ELGEN, with a node increment of 100 and an element increment of 12, resulting in a total of 2 elements through the thickness and 24 structured brick elements overall. The concentrated load is applied at the center of the top surface using the existing top-center node at coordinates 0, 0, 1. In this model, that node is node 201. The load is applied using CLOAD in the U3 direction, producing a downward point load at the center of the disc.
The material is modeled as linear elastic with a Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and a Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:  3 Point Bending of a beam under displacement loading
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: beam_under_flexural_loading
case material: metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the bending response of a simply supported beam under three point bending using beam elements in Abaqus Standard.
The beam has a total length of 100 mm with a rectangular cross section of 30 mm by 15 mm. The support span is 50 mm, with supports located at 25 mm and 75 mm along the beam length, and a displacement load applied at the midspan at 50 mm.
The beam is discretized using a structured one dimensional mesh of B23 beam elements. Nodes are defined at the two ends of the beam and NGEN is used to generate intermediate nodes, creating a total of 21 nodes along the beam axis. The beam length is divided into 20 equal elements, giving a uniform element size of 5 mm. This mesh is selected such that nodes exist exactly at the support locations and at the midspan, allowing boundary conditions and loading to be applied directly at nodal positions. A single seed beam element is defined and replicated along the beam using ELGEN.
The cross section is defined using a rectangular beam section with the specified dimensions, and the material is modeled as linear elastic.
Boundary conditions represent simple supports at the two support locations. The transverse displacement U2 is constrained at both supports, while axial displacement U1 is constrained at only one support to prevent rigid body motion without introducing artificial axial restraint. A prescribed downward displacement is applied at the midspan node.
The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the bending response of the beam under displacement controlled three point bending using a structured beam element formulation.
</problem_description>

The beam is discretized using a structured one dimensional mesh of B23 beam elements. The beam length is divided into 20 equal elements, giving a uniform element size of 5 mm. A single seed beam element is defined and replicated along the beam using ELGEN.

Boundary conditions represent simple supports at the two support locations. The transverse displacement U2 is constrained at both supports, while axial displacement U1 is constrained at only one support to prevent rigid body motion without introducing artificial axial restraint.
Two equal downward concentrated forces are applied at the loading points, producing a region of constant bending moment between them.
The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the bending response of the beam under symmetric four point bending using a structured beam element formulation.

<problem_description>
This model analyzes the bending response of a cantilever beam subjected to a point load using beam elements in Abaqus Standard.
The beam has a total length of 100 mm with a rectangular cross section of 30 mm by 15 mm. One end of the beam at x = 0 mm is fully fixed, while the other end is free.
The beam is discretized using a structured one dimensional mesh of B23 beam elements. Nodes are defined at the two ends of the beam and NGEN is used to generate intermediate nodes, resulting in a total of 21 nodes along the beam axis. The beam length is divided into 20 equal elements, giving a uniform element size of 5 mm. A single seed beam element is defined and replicated along the beam using ELGEN to obtain a uniform mesh.
The cross section is defined using a rectangular beam section, and the material is modeled as linear elastic.
Boundary conditions represent a clamped support at the left end of the beam by constraining axial displacement U1, transverse displacement U2, and rotation UR3. The right end of the beam remains free.
A concentrated point load is applied at the other end of the beam (x=100) in the transverse direction using the CLOAD definition.
The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the deflection and bending response of the cantilever beam under point loading using a structured beam element formulation.

<index>
case name: Simply supported beam under distributed loading  
case domain: staticstressdisplacementanalysis_bending
case category: beam_under_flexural_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the bending response of a simply supported beam subjected to a uniformly distributed transverse load using beam elements in Abaqus Standard.
The beam has a total length of 100 mm and a rectangular cross section of 30 mm by 15 mm. The geometry is defined along a single spatial dimension, with nodes generated from x = 0 mm to x = 100 mm.
The beam is discretized using B23 beam elements. Two end nodes are defined and NGEN is used to generate intermediate nodes, resulting in 21 nodes along the length. A single beam element is defined and replicated using ELGEN to create a uniform mesh of 20 elements, each of length 5 mm.
A rectangular beam section is assigned to all elements, and the material is modeled as linear elastic.
Simply supported boundary conditions are applied at the two ends of the beam. At the left end (x = 0 mm), axial displacement U1 and transverse displacement U2 are constrained. At the right end (x = 100 mm), only transverse displacement U2 is constrained. This combination prevents rigid body motion while allowing axial expansion, consistent with a pin-roller support condition.
A uniformly distributed load is applied over the entire beam length in the transverse direction using a beam load definition (P2), producing bending deformation.
The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the deflection and internal force response of the simply supported beam under distributed loading using a structured beam element formulation.
</problem_description>

<index>
case name: Buckling analysis of a simply supported beam under axial compression  
case domain: bucklinganalysis
case category: beam_under_axial_loading
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model predicts the elastic buckling behavior of a simply supported beam subjected to axial compressive loading using an eigenvalue buckling analysis in Abaqus Standard.
The beam has a total length of 100 mm and a rectangular cross section of 30 mm by 15 mm. The geometry is defined along a single spatial dimension, with nodes generated from x = 0 mm to x = 100 mm.
The beam is discretized using B23 beam elements. Two end nodes are defined and NGEN is used to generate intermediate nodes, resulting in 21 nodes along the beam axis. A single beam element is defined and replicated using ELGEN to create a uniform mesh of 20 elements.
A rectangular beam section is assigned to all elements, and the material is modeled as linear elastic.
Simply supported boundary conditions are applied at the two ends. At the left end (x = 0 mm), axial displacement U1 and transverse displacement U2 are constrained. At the right end (x = 100 mm), only transverse displacement U2 is constrained. This pin-roller configuration allows axial shortening while preventing rigid body motion.
A reference axial compressive load is applied at the right end in the beam axial direction (U1).
The analysis is performed using a perturbation step with the *BUCKLE procedure, which solves a linear eigenvalue problem based on the preloaded configuration. This approach computes the buckling load multipliers and corresponding mode shapes without requiring geometric imperfections or nonlinear analysis.
The objective of the simulation is to determine the critical buckling load and associated mode shapes of the beam.
</problem_description>

case category: beam_under_flexural_loading 
case material: metal
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the free vibration behavior of a simply supported beam using a modal (frequency extraction) analysis in Abaqus Standard.
The beam has a total length of 100 mm and a rectangular cross section of 30 mm by 15 mm. The geometry is defined along a single spatial dimension, with nodes generated from x = 0 mm to x = 100 mm.
The beam is discretized using B23 beam elements. Two end nodes are defined and NGEN is used to generate intermediate nodes, resulting in 21 nodes along the beam axis. A single beam element is defined and replicated using ELGEN to create a uniform mesh of 20 elements.
A rectangular beam section is assigned to all elements. The material is modeled as linear elastic and includes density to account for inertial effects required in modal analysis.
Simply supported boundary conditions are applied at the two ends. At the left end (x = 0 mm), axial displacement U1 and transverse displacement U2 are constrained. At the right end (x = 100 mm), only transverse displacement U2 is constrained. This pin-roller configuration allows axial motion while preventing rigid body translation.
The analysis is performed using the *FREQUENCY procedure, which extracts the natural frequencies and corresponding mode shapes of the structure by solving an eigenvalue problem involving the mass and stiffness matrices.
The objective of the simulation is to determine the natural frequencies and mode shapes of the beam. The first mode corresponds to a half-sine bending shape, with higher modes showing increasing numbers of half-waves along the beam length.
</problem_description>

case category:hollow_column_under_axial_loading 
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the axial stress and deformation response of a hollow circular pipe using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The pipe has a length of 100 mm, an outer diameter of 20 mm, and an inner diameter of 15 mm. One end of the pipe is fully clamped, and a uniform pressure is applied on the opposite end face.

The geometry is modeled as a full 3D solid aligned along the global Z-axis. The circular cross section is approximated using a structured annular topology with 8 circumferential sectors. Each cross section consists of 16 nodes: 8 nodes on the inner radius and 8 nodes on the outer radius, arranged in a clockwise order. This allows the annular region to be represented using 8 mapped quadrilateral sectors, each of which forms the base of a hexahedral element.

The mesh generation follows a partially structured keyword-based approach. Two full cross-sectional node layers are defined explicitly at Z = 0 mm and Z = 100 mm. Intermediate node layers are generated using NGEN, where each node is propagated along the axial direction with a consistent node increment of 100. This produces 11 node layers and therefore 10 element layers along the pipe length.

The element topology is based on a valid 8-element seed layer defined between Z = 0 and Z = 10 mm. Each element corresponds to one annular sector and is constructed using a consistent bottom-face to top-face node ordering. This seed layer was verified independently to ensure positive element volumes and correct orientation.

Unlike the solid rod case, ELGEN is not used to generate the full mesh. Although the node generation remains fully structured, attempts to propagate the seed elements using ELGEN resulted in negative-volume elements due to sensitivity of annular sector connectivity to node ordering and orientation. This highlights an important limitation: ELGEN works reliably when the seed element topology aligns naturally with the structured coordinate directions, but can fail for geometries like hollow pipes where the circumferential topology introduces orientation ambiguity.

To maintain robustness and clarity, the full element connectivity is therefore defined explicitly for all 10 axial layers. The pattern follows a consistent layer-by-layer replication of the validated seed element configuration. The final mesh consists of 80 C3D8R elements arranged as 8 sectors circumferentially and 10 elements along the length.

The material is defined as linear elastic with Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

Boundary conditions are applied by fully constraining all nodes on the Z = 0 mm end face, fixing U1, U2, and U3 to represent a clamped support. The opposite end face is subjected to a uniform pressure load applied through an element-based surface definition. The loaded surface is defined using an ELSET corresponding to the last element layer. The correct face label is determined based on the element connectivity and should be verified in the Visualization module.

A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the axial response of a hollow pipe under pressure loading, while demonstrating a structured keyword-based modeling strategy and highlighting practical limitations of ELGEN for annular geometries.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:ONE END CLAMPED 3D SOLID ROD UNDER AXIAL PRESSURE LOADING 
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_tension
case category:solid_column_under_axial_loading
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model represents the axial tension response of a solid circular rod using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The rod has a length of 100 mm and a diameter of 20 mm, and is loaded by applying a uniform pressure on one end while the opposite end is fully clamped.

The geometry is modeled as a full 3D solid rod aligned along the global Z-axis. The circular cross section is not generated using automatic meshing but is instead constructed using a structured, block-based topology consisting of a center node, an inner ring of 8 nodes, and an outer ring of 8 nodes. This results in 17 nodes per cross section and allows the circular domain to be approximated using 12 mapped quadrilateral regions.

The mesh generation strategy is entirely keyword-driven and highly structured. Two full cross-sectional node layers are defined explicitly at Z = 0 mm and Z = 100 mm. Each node on the bottom surface has a corresponding node on the top surface with a consistent numbering offset of 1000. Intermediate node layers along the length are generated using multiple NGEN commands, each applied to corresponding node pairs between the two end faces. The node increment between adjacent cross sections is 100, resulting in 11 total node layers and 10 element layers along the rod length.

The element mesh is built by first defining 12 seed C3D8R elements in the initial cross-sectional layer between Z = 0 and Z = 10 mm. These elements are arranged to fill the circular cross section using the center node, inner ring, and outer ring topology. The full 3D mesh is then generated using ELGEN by extruding each of these 12 seed elements along the Z-direction for 10 layers. The node increment per layer is 100 and the element increment per layer is 12, resulting in a total of 120 brick elements. The mesh is fully structured and consistent along the axial direction.

An important aspect of the topology is that the circular cross section is approximated using a small number of structured blocks rather than true curved elements. The validity of the entire mesh depends on the correct node ordering of the seed elements, as ELGEN directly propagates this connectivity. The element face labels used for loading are therefore determined by this initial ordering.

The material is defined as a linear elastic solid with Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

Boundary conditions are applied by fully constraining all nodes on the bottom end face (Z = 0 mm), fixing U1, U2, and U3 to represent a clamped condition. The top end face (Z = 100 mm) is subjected to a uniformly distributed axial pressure acting in the negative Z-direction. The loaded surface is defined using an ELSET corresponding to the last layer of elements, and a SURFACE definition is created from these elements. The correct face label for the loaded surface is S2, which is determined based on the seed element node ordering.

A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the axial stress and deformation response of the rod under tensile pressure loading, and to demonstrate a clean, structured keyword-based approach for modeling a solid circular geometry using NGEN and ELGEN.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:ONE END CLAMPED 3D HOLLOW PIPE UNDER TORSIONAL LOADING AT OTHER END  
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_torsion 
case category:shaft_with_torsion_loading 
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model analyzes the torsional response of a hollow circular pipe using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The pipe has a length of 100 mm, an outer diameter of 20 mm, and an inner diameter of 15 mm. One end of the pipe is fully clamped, and torsion is applied at the opposite end through a prescribed rotation.
The geometry is modeled as a full 3D solid aligned along the global Z-axis. The circular cross section is approximated using a structured annular topology consisting of 8 circumferential sectors. Each cross section contains 16 nodes: 8 nodes on the inner radius and 8 nodes on the outer radius. These nodes are arranged in a consistent clockwise order, allowing the annular region to be discretized into 8 mapped quadrilateral sectors, each forming the base of a hexahedral element.
The mesh generation follows a partially structured keyword-based approach. Two full cross-sectional node layers are defined explicitly at Z = 0 mm and Z = 100 mm. Intermediate node layers are generated using NGEN, where each node is propagated along the axial direction with a constant node increment of 100. This produces 11 node layers and therefore 10 element layers along the pipe length.
The element topology is based on a validated 8-element seed layer defined between Z = 0 and Z = 10 mm. Each element represents one annular sector and is constructed using a consistent bottom-face to top-face node ordering, similar to the approach used in the solid rod case. This seed layer was independently verified to ensure correct element orientation and positive volume.
Unlike the solid rod model, ELGEN is not used to generate the full mesh. Although the node generation is fully structured, attempts to propagate the seed elements using ELGEN resulted in negative-volume elements. This occurs because annular sector elements are sensitive to circumferential orientation, and the topology does not align with a simple directional replication scheme. This highlights an important limitation: ELGEN works well for geometries with orthogonal or radially symmetric block structures, but may fail for hollow geometries where element orientation depends on angular consistency.
To ensure robustness, the full element connectivity is defined explicitly for all axial layers. The mesh is constructed by repeating the verified seed pattern layer by layer, resulting in a total of 80 C3D8R elements arranged as 8 sectors circumferentially and 10 elements along the length.
The material is defined as linear elastic with Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.
Boundary conditions are applied by fully constraining all nodes on the Z = 0 mm end face, fixing U1, U2, and U3 to represent a clamped support. The torsional load is applied using a reference point located at the center of the free end (Z = 100 mm). This reference point is not connected to the mesh but is coupled kinematically to the end surface using a surface-based coupling constraint. The reference point is constrained in all translational degrees of freedom and in two rotational degrees of freedom, while a prescribed rotation is applied about the pipe axis (UR3). This approach enforces a uniform twist across the end face and avoids inconsistencies associated with applying nodal moments directly.
A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the stress and deformation response of a hollow pipe under torsional loading, while demonstrating a structured keyword-based modeling strategy and highlighting practical limitations of ELGEN for annular geometries.
</problem_description>

<case_begin>
<index>
case name:ONE END CLAMPED 3D SOLID ROD UNDER TORSIONAL LOADING AT THE FREE END   
case domain:staticstressdisplacementanalysis_torsion 
case category:shaft_with_torsion_loading 
case material:metal 
</index>
<file_content>
<problem_description>
This model represents the torsional response of a solid circular rod using a 3D continuum formulation in Abaqus Standard. The rod has a length of 100 mm and a diameter of 20 mm. One end is clamped, and torsion is applied at the opposite end by prescribing a rotational degree of freedom to a reference point that is kinematically coupled to the end face.

The geometry is modeled as a full 3D solid rod aligned with the global Z-axis. As in the axial loading version of the model, the circular cross section is constructed using a structured block-style topology rather than automatic free meshing. Each cross section contains 17 nodes: 1 center node, 8 inner-ring nodes, and 8 outer-ring nodes. This arrangement allows the circular area to be partitioned into 12 mapped quadrilateral regions, which are then used as the basis for the 3D solid mesh.

The mesh generation is fully keyword-based. Two complete cross-sectional node layers are defined explicitly, one at Z = 0 mm and the other at Z = 100 mm. Intermediate node layers are generated along the rod axis using multiple NGEN commands, each connecting corresponding nodes on the two end sections. The node increment between adjacent cross sections is 100, producing 11 node layers in total and therefore 10 element layers along the rod length.

The element mesh is created by first defining 12 seed C3D8R elements in the first axial segment of the rod. These seed elements fill the circular cross section using the center, inner-ring, and outer-ring topology. ELGEN is then used to extrude each of these seed elements along the Z-direction through 10 layers. The node increment between element layers is 100 and the element increment between layers is 12, resulting in a total of 120 structured brick elements for the full rod.

An important modeling detail is that the loaded end face is not directly given a distributed traction or moment. Instead, the last element layer is collected into an ELSET, and an element-based surface is defined on the end face. For this element connectivity, the end face corresponds to face S2. A kinematic coupling is then used to tie this end surface to a reference point. This means the free-end face behaves as a rigidly controlled section for loading purposes, allowing a prescribed rotation to be applied cleanly through the reference point.

The material is defined as linear elastic with Young’s modulus of 70000 MPa and Poisson’s ratio of 0.3.

Boundary conditions are applied by fully constraining all nodes on the Z = 0 mm end face, fixing U1, U2, and U3 to represent a clamped support. At the loading end, the reference point associated with the coupled end surface is constrained in translations and in two rotations, while the torsional rotation is prescribed through the rotational degree of freedom about the rod axis. In this input, the reference point is fixed in DOFs 1 through 5, and a value is prescribed for DOF 6 to impose the twist. This loading strategy is more suitable for torsion than applying nodal moments directly to the end-face nodes, because it enforces a consistent rotation of the coupled face.

A static analysis step is used with small deformation assumptions. The objective of the simulation is to evaluate the stress and deformation response of the solid rod under torsional loading, while demonstrating a clean structured keyword-based modeling approach for a circular 3D solid using NGEN, ELGEN, an element surface, and a reference-point kinematic coupling.
</problem_description>
